   <h1 id="firstHeading" class="firstHeading">Antigua and Barbuda</h1> 
   <div id="bodyContent" class="vector-body"> 
    <div id="siteSub" class="noprint">
     From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia
    </div> 
    <div id="contentSub"></div> 
    <div id="contentSub2"></div> 
    <div id="jump-to-nav"></div> <a class="mw-jump-link" href="#mw-head">Jump to navigation</a> <a class="mw-jump-link" href="#searchInput">Jump to search</a> 
    <div id="mw-content-text" class="mw-body-content mw-content-ltr" lang="en" dir="ltr">
     <div class="mw-parser-output">
      <div class="shortdescription nomobile noexcerpt noprint searchaux" style="display:none">
       Country in the West Indies in the Americas
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       This article is about the sovereign country in West Indies. For the islands of the sovereign state, see <a href="/wiki/Antigua" title="Antigua">Antigua</a> and <a href="/wiki/Barbuda" title="Barbuda">Barbuda</a>. For other uses, see <a href="/wiki/Antigua_(disambiguation)" class="mw-disambig" title="Antigua (disambiguation)">Antigua (disambiguation)</a> and <a href="/wiki/Barbuda_(disambiguation)" class="mw-disambig" title="Barbuda (disambiguation)">Barbuda (disambiguation)</a>.
      </div>

      <p><b>Antigua and Barbuda</b> (<span class="rt-commentedText nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/æ/: 'a' in 'bad'">æ</span><span title="'n' in 'nigh'">n</span><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="'t' in 'tie'">t</span><span title="/iː/: 'ee' in 'fleece'">iː</span><span title="/ɡ/: 'g' in 'guy'">ɡ</span></span>(<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="'w' in 'wind'">w</span></span>)<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ə/: 'a' in 'about'">ə</span></span> ...<span class="wrap"> </span><span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="'b' in 'buy'">b</span><span title="/ɑːr/: 'ar' in 'far'">ɑːr</span><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="'b' in 'buy'">b</span></span>(<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/j/: 'y' in 'yes'">j</span></span>)<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/uː/: 'oo' in 'goose'">uː</span><span title="'d' in 'dye'">d</span><span title="/ə/: 'a' in 'about'">ə</span></span>/</a></span> <span class="nowrap" style="font-size:85%">(<span class="unicode haudio"><span class="fn"><span style="white-space:nowrap;margin-right:.25em;"><a href="/wiki/File:En-us-Antiga_and_Barbuda.ogg" title="About this sound"><img alt="About this sound" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/11px-Loudspeaker.svg.png" decoding="async" width="11" height="11" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/17px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/22px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="20" data-file-height="20"></a></span><a href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/4/47/En-us-Antigua_and_Barbuda-2.oga" class="internal" title="En-us-Antiga and Barbuda.ogg">listen</a></span></span>)</span></span>; <a href="/wiki/Help:Pronunciation_respelling_key" title="Help:Pronunciation respelling key"><i title="English pronunciation respelling">an-<span style="font-size:90%">TEE</span>-g(w)ə ... bar-<span style="font-size:90%">B(Y)OO</span>-də</i></a>) is a <a href="/wiki/Sovereign_state" title="Sovereign state">sovereign</a> <a href="/wiki/Island_country" title="Island country">island country</a> in the <a href="/wiki/West_Indies" title="West Indies">West Indies</a> in the Americas, lying between the <a href="/wiki/Caribbean_Sea" title="Caribbean Sea">Caribbean Sea</a> and the Atlantic Ocean. It consists of two major islands, <a href="/wiki/Antigua" title="Antigua">Antigua</a> and <a href="/wiki/Barbuda" title="Barbuda">Barbuda</a> separated by 63&nbsp;km (39&nbsp;mi), and smaller islands (including <a href="/wiki/Great_Bird_Island,_Antigua" class="mw-redirect" title="Great Bird Island, Antigua">Great Bird</a>, <a href="/wiki/Green_Island_(Antigua_and_Barbuda)" title="Green Island (Antigua and Barbuda)">Green</a>, <a href="/wiki/Guiana_Island" title="Guiana Island">Guiana</a>, <a href="/wiki/Long_Island_(Antigua_and_Barbuda)" title="Long Island (Antigua and Barbuda)">Long</a>, <a href="/wiki/Maiden_Island_(Antigua_and_Barbuda)" title="Maiden Island (Antigua and Barbuda)">Maiden</a>, <a href="/wiki/Prickly_Pear_Island" title="Prickly Pear Island">Prickly Pear</a>, <a href="/wiki/York_Island_(Antigua_and_Barbuda)" title="York Island (Antigua and Barbuda)">York Islands</a>, <a href="/wiki/Redonda" title="Redonda">Redonda</a>). The permanent population number is about 97,120 (2019 est.), with 97% being resident on Antigua.<sup id="cite_ref-Factbook_1-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Factbook-1">[1]</a></sup> The capital and largest port and city is <a href="/wiki/St._John%27s,_Antigua_and_Barbuda" title="St. John's, Antigua and Barbuda">St. John's</a> on Antigua, with <a href="/wiki/Codrington,_Antigua_and_Barbuda" title="Codrington, Antigua and Barbuda">Codrington</a> being the largest town on Barbuda. Lying near each other, Antigua and Barbuda are in the middle of the <a href="/wiki/Leeward_Islands" title="Leeward Islands">Leeward Islands</a>, part of the <a href="/wiki/Lesser_Antilles" title="Lesser Antilles">Lesser Antilles</a>, roughly at <a href="/wiki/17th_parallel_north" title="17th parallel north">17°N</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Equator" title="Equator">equator</a>. </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Antigua" title="Antigua">island of Antigua</a> was explored by <a href="/wiki/Christopher_Columbus" title="Christopher Columbus">Christopher Columbus</a> in 1493 and named for the <a href="/wiki/Santa_Mar%C3%ADa_La_Antigua" title="Santa María La Antigua">Church of Santa María La Antigua</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Crocker,_John_1968_6-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Crocker,_John_1968-6">[6]</a></sup> Antigua was colonized by Britain in 1632; <a href="/wiki/Barbuda" title="Barbuda">Barbuda</a> island was first colonised in 1678.<sup id="cite_ref-Crocker,_John_1968_6-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Crocker,_John_1968-6">[6]</a></sup> Having been part of the <a href="/wiki/British_Leeward_Islands" title="British Leeward Islands">Federal Colony of the Leeward Islands</a> from 1871, Antigua and Barbuda joined the <a href="/wiki/West_Indies_Federation" title="West Indies Federation">West Indies Federation</a> in 1958.<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup> With the breakup of the federation, it became one of the <a href="/wiki/West_Indies_Associated_States" title="West Indies Associated States">West Indies Associated States</a> in 1967.<sup id="cite_ref-Sheridan1974_8-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Sheridan1974-8">[8]</a></sup> Following self-governance in its internal affairs, independence was granted from the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">United Kingdom</a> on 1 November 1981. Antigua and Barbuda is a member of the <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_of_Nations" title="Commonwealth of Nations">Commonwealth</a> and <a href="/wiki/Elizabeth_II" title="Elizabeth II">Elizabeth II</a> is the country's queen and <a href="/wiki/Head_of_state" title="Head of state">head of state</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The economy of Antigua and Barbuda is particularly dependent on tourism, which accounts for 80% of GDP. <a href="/wiki/Effects_of_climate_change_on_island_nations" title="Effects of climate change on island nations">Like other island nations</a>, Antigua and Barbuda are particularly vulnerable to the effects of Earth having an atmosphere, such as <a href="/wiki/Sea_level_rise" title="Sea level rise">sea level rise</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Extreme_weather" title="Extreme weather">increased intensity of extreme weather</a> like hurricanes, which have direct impacts on the island through coastal erosion, <a href="/wiki/Water_scarcity" title="Water scarcity">water scarcity</a>, and other challenges.<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup> As of 2019, Antigua and Barbuda has a 0% individual income tax rate,<sup id="cite_ref-auto1_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto1-11">[11]</a></sup> as does neighboring <a href="/wiki/Saint_Kitts_and_Nevis" title="Saint Kitts and Nevis">St. Kitts and Nevis</a>. </p>

      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology">Etymology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Antigua_and_Barbuda&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Etymology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <p><i><i lang="es" title="Spanish-language text">Antigua</i></i> is Spanish for "ancient" and <i><i lang="es" title="Spanish-language text">barbuda</i></i> is Spanish for "bearded".<sup id="cite_ref-Factbook_1-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Factbook-1">[1]</a></sup> The island of Antigua was originally called <i><i lang="tnq" title="Taino-language text">Wadadli</i></i> by <a href="/wiki/Arawak" title="Arawak">Arawaks</a> and is locally known by that name today; <a href="/wiki/Island_Caribs" class="mw-redirect" title="Island Caribs">Caribs</a> possibly called Barbuda <i><i lang="crb" title="Island Carib-language text">Wa'omoni</i></i>. <a href="/wiki/Christopher_Columbus" title="Christopher Columbus">Christopher Columbus</a>, while sailing by in 1493 may have named it Santa Maria la Antigua, after an icon in the Spanish <a href="/wiki/Seville_Cathedral" title="Seville Cathedral">Seville Cathedral</a>. The "bearded" of Barbuda is thought to refer either to the male inhabitants of the island, or the bearded fig trees present there. </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Antigua_and_Barbuda&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_Antigua_and_Barbuda" title="History of Antigua and Barbuda">History of Antigua and Barbuda</a>
      </div> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Pre-colonial_period">Pre-colonial period</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Antigua_and_Barbuda&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Pre-colonial period">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>Antigua was first settled by archaic age hunter-gatherer <a href="/wiki/Amerindian" class="mw-redirect" title="Amerindian">Amerindians</a> called the <a href="/wiki/Ciboney" title="Ciboney">Ciboney</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Factbook_1-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Factbook-1">[1]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Britannica_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Britannica-12">[12]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Commonwealth_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Commonwealth-13">[13]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Radiocarbon_dating" title="Radiocarbon dating">Carbon dating</a> has established the earliest settlements started around 3100 BC.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2019)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> They were succeeded by the ceramic age pre-Columbian <a href="/wiki/Arawakan_languages" title="Arawakan languages">Arawak</a>-speaking <a href="/wiki/Saladoid" title="Saladoid">Saladoid</a> people who migrated from the lower <a href="/wiki/Orinoco_River" class="mw-redirect" title="Orinoco River">Orinoco River</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2019)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> They introduced agriculture, raising, among other crops, the famous Antigua black pineapple (<i><a href="/wiki/Ananas_comosus" class="mw-redirect" title="Ananas comosus">Ananas comosus</a></i>), <a href="/wiki/Maize" title="Maize">corn</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sweet_potato" title="Sweet potato">sweet potatoes</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chili_pepper" title="Chili pepper">chiles</a>, <a href="/wiki/Guava" title="Guava">guava</a>, tobacco, and cotton.<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup> Later on the more bellicose <a href="/wiki/Island_Caribs" class="mw-redirect" title="Island Caribs">Caribs</a> also settled the island, possibly by force. </p> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:The_Mill_Yard_-_Ten_Views_in_the_Island_of_Antigua_(1823),_plate_V_-_BL.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/The_Mill_Yard_-_Ten_Views_in_the_Island_of_Antigua_%281823%29%2C_plate_V_-_BL.jpg/220px-The_Mill_Yard_-_Ten_Views_in_the_Island_of_Antigua_%281823%29%2C_plate_V_-_BL.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="153" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/The_Mill_Yard_-_Ten_Views_in_the_Island_of_Antigua_%281823%29%2C_plate_V_-_BL.jpg/330px-The_Mill_Yard_-_Ten_Views_in_the_Island_of_Antigua_%281823%29%2C_plate_V_-_BL.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/The_Mill_Yard_-_Ten_Views_in_the_Island_of_Antigua_%281823%29%2C_plate_V_-_BL.jpg/440px-The_Mill_Yard_-_Ten_Views_in_the_Island_of_Antigua_%281823%29%2C_plate_V_-_BL.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1784" data-file-height="1241"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:The_Mill_Yard_-_Ten_Views_in_the_Island_of_Antigua_(1823),_plate_V_-_BL.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Antigua in 1823
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="European_arrival_and_settlement">European arrival and settlement</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Antigua_and_Barbuda&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: European arrival and settlement">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p><a href="/wiki/Christopher_Columbus" title="Christopher Columbus">Christopher Columbus</a> was the first European to sight the islands in 1493.<sup id="cite_ref-Britannica_12-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Britannica-12">[12]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Commonwealth_13-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Commonwealth-13">[13]</a></sup> The Spanish did not colonise Antigua until after a combination of European and African diseases, malnutrition, and slavery eventually extirpated most of the native population; <a href="/wiki/Smallpox" title="Smallpox">smallpox</a> was probably the greatest killer.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The English settled on Antigua in 1632;<sup id="cite_ref-Commonwealth_13-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Commonwealth-13">[13]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Britannica_12-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Britannica-12">[12]</a></sup> Christopher Codrington settled on Barbuda in 1685.<sup id="cite_ref-Commonwealth_13-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Commonwealth-13">[13]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Britannica_12-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Britannica-12">[12]</a></sup> Tobacco and then sugar was grown, worked by a large population of slaves from West Africa who soon came to vastly outnumber the European settlers.<sup id="cite_ref-Britannica_12-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Britannica-12">[12]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Colonial_era">Colonial era</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Antigua_and_Barbuda&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Colonial era">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>The English maintained control of the islands, repulsing an attempted French attack in 1666.<sup id="cite_ref-Britannica_12-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Britannica-12">[12]</a></sup> The brutal conditions endured by the slaves led to revolts in 1701 and 1729 and a planned revolt in 1736, the last led by <a href="/w/index.php?title=Prince_Klaas&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Prince Klaas (page does not exist)">Prince Klaas</a>, though it was discovered before it began and the ringleaders were executed.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Slavery" title="Slavery">Slavery</a> was abolished in the British Empire in 1833, affecting the economy.<sup id="cite_ref-Commonwealth_13-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Commonwealth-13">[13]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Britannica_12-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Britannica-12">[12]</a></sup> This was exacerbated by natural disasters such as the 1843 earthquake and the 1847 hurricane.<sup id="cite_ref-Britannica_12-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Britannica-12">[12]</a></sup> Mining occurred on the isle of <a href="/wiki/Redonda" title="Redonda">Redonda</a>, however this ceased in 1929 and the island has since remained uninhabited.<sup id="cite_ref-kras-2008_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-kras-2008-17">[17]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Part of the Leeward Islands colony, Antigua and Barbuda became part of the short-lived <a href="/wiki/West_Indies_Federation" title="West Indies Federation">West Indies Federation</a> from 1958 to 1962.<sup id="cite_ref-Commonwealth_13-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Commonwealth-13">[13]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Britannica_12-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Britannica-12">[12]</a></sup> Antigua and Barbuda subsequently became an associated state of the United Kingdom with full internal autonomy on 27 February 1967.<sup id="cite_ref-Britannica_12-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Britannica-12">[12]</a></sup> The 1970s were dominated by discussions as to the islands' future and the rivalry between <a href="/wiki/Vere_Bird" title="Vere Bird">Vere Bird</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Antigua_Labour_Party" class="mw-redirect" title="Antigua Labour Party">Antigua Labour Party</a> (ALP) (Premier from 1967 to 1971 and 1976 to 1981) and the <a href="/wiki/Progressive_Labour_Movement" title="Progressive Labour Movement">Progressive Labour Movement</a> (PLM) of <a href="/wiki/George_Walter" title="George Walter">George Walter</a> (Premier 1971–1976). Eventually Antigua and Barbuda gained full independence on 1 November 1981; Vere Bird became Prime Minister of the new country.<sup id="cite_ref-Britannica_12-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Britannica-12">[12]</a></sup> The country opted to remain within the <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_of_Nations" title="Commonwealth of Nations">Commonwealth</a>, retaining Queen Elizabeth as <a href="/wiki/Monarchy_of_Antigua_and_Barbuda" title="Monarchy of Antigua and Barbuda">head of state</a>, with the last <a href="/wiki/List_of_colonial_governors_and_administrators_of_Antigua#Governors_of_Antigua_and_Barbuda_(1967–1981)" title="List of colonial governors and administrators of Antigua">Governor</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wilfred_Jacobs" title="Wilfred Jacobs">Sir Wilfred Jacobs</a>, as <a href="/wiki/Governor-General_of_Antigua_and_Barbuda" title="Governor-General of Antigua and Barbuda">Governor-General</a>. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Independence_era">Independence era</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Antigua_and_Barbuda&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Independence era">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>The first two decades of Antigua's independence were dominated politically by the Bird family and the ALP, with Vere Bird ruling from 1981 to 1994, followed by his son <a href="/wiki/Lester_Bird" title="Lester Bird">Lester Bird</a> from 1994 to 2004.<sup id="cite_ref-Britannica_12-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Britannica-12">[12]</a></sup> Though providing a degree of political stability, and boosting tourism to the country, the Bird governments were frequently accused of corruption, cronyism and financial malfeasance.<sup id="cite_ref-Commonwealth_13-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Commonwealth-13">[13]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Britannica_12-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Britannica-12">[12]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Vere_Bird_Jr." title="Vere Bird Jr.">Vere Bird Jr.</a>, the elder son, was forced to leave the cabinet in 1990 following a <a href="/wiki/Guns_for_Antigua" title="Guns for Antigua">scandal</a> in which he was accused of smuggling Israeli weapons to Colombian drug-traffickers.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Commonwealth_13-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Commonwealth-13">[13]</a></sup> Another son, <a href="/wiki/Ivor_Bird" title="Ivor Bird">Ivor Bird</a>, was convicted of selling <a href="/wiki/Cocaine" title="Cocaine">cocaine</a> in 1995.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In 1995 <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Luis" title="Hurricane Luis">Hurricane Luis</a> caused severe damage on Barbuda.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The ALP's dominance of Antiguan politics ended with the <a href="/wiki/2004_Antiguan_general_election" title="2004 Antiguan general election">2004 Antiguan general election</a>, which was won by <a href="/wiki/Baldwin_Spencer" title="Baldwin Spencer">Baldwin Spencer</a>'s <a href="/wiki/United_Progressive_Party_(Antigua_and_Barbuda)" title="United Progressive Party (Antigua and Barbuda)">United Progressive Party</a> (UPP).<sup id="cite_ref-Britannica_12-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Britannica-12">[12]</a></sup> However the UPP lost the <a href="/wiki/2014_Antiguan_general_election" title="2014 Antiguan general election">2014 Antiguan general election</a>, with the ALP returning to power under <a href="/wiki/Gaston_Browne" title="Gaston Browne">Gaston Browne</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-bald_23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bald-23">[23]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Most of Barbuda was devastated in early September 2017 by <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Irma" title="Hurricane Irma">Hurricane Irma</a>, which brought winds with speeds reaching 295&nbsp;km/h (185&nbsp;mph). The storm damaged or destroyed 95% of the island's buildings and infrastructure, leaving Barbuda "barely habitable" according to Prime Minister Gaston Browne. Nearly everyone on the island was evacuated to Antigua.<sup id="cite_ref-auto_24-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto-24">[24]</a></sup> Amidst the following rebuilding efforts on Barbuda that were estimated to cost at least $100 million,<sup id="cite_ref-time.com_25-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-time.com-25">[25]</a></sup> the government announced plans to revoke a century old law of <a href="/wiki/Communal_land" title="Communal land">communal land ownership</a> by allowing residents to buy land; a move that has been criticised as promoting "disaster capitalism".<sup id="cite_ref-NACLA-disaster-capitalism_26-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NACLA-disaster-capitalism-26">[26]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Antigua_and_Barbuda&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Geography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Geography_of_Antigua_and_Barbuda" title="Geography of Antigua and Barbuda">Geography of Antigua and Barbuda</a>
      </div> 
      <style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r997900035">.mw-parser-output .locmap .od{position:absolute}.mw-parser-output .locmap .id{position:absolute;line-height:0}.mw-parser-output .locmap .l0{font-size:0;position:absolute}.mw-parser-output .locmap .pv{line-height:110%;position:absolute;text-align:center}.mw-parser-output .locmap .pl{line-height:110%;position:absolute;top:-0.75em;text-align:right}.mw-parser-output .locmap .pr{line-height:110%;position:absolute;top:-0.75em;text-align:left}.mw-parser-output .locmap .pv>div{display:inline;padding:1px}.mw-parser-output .locmap .pl>div{display:inline;padding:1px;float:right}.mw-parser-output .locmap .pr>div{display:inline;padding:1px;float:left}</style>
      <div class="locmap noviewer thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px">

      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Antigue_34622.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/Antigue_34622.jpg/220px-Antigue_34622.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="124" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/Antigue_34622.jpg/330px-Antigue_34622.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/Antigue_34622.jpg/440px-Antigue_34622.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3968" data-file-height="2232"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Antigue_34622.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>English Harbour, Antigua
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Antigua and Barbuda both are generally low-lying islands whose terrain has been influenced more by <a href="/wiki/Limestone" title="Limestone">limestone</a> formations than <a href="/wiki/Volcanism" title="Volcanism">volcanic activity</a>. The highest point on Antigua and Barbuda is <a href="/wiki/Boggy_Peak" title="Boggy Peak">Boggy Peak</a>, located in southwestern Antigua, which is the remnant of a <a href="/wiki/Volcanic" class="mw-redirect" title="Volcanic">volcanic</a> crater rising 402 metres (1,319 feet).<sup id="cite_ref-Factbook_1-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Factbook-1">[1]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Britannica_12-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Britannica-12">[12]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The shorelines of both islands are greatly indented with beaches, lagoons, and natural harbors. The islands are rimmed by reefs and shoals. There are few streams as rainfall is slight. Both islands lack adequate amounts of fresh groundwater.<sup id="cite_ref-Factbook_1-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Factbook-1">[1]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>About 40&nbsp;km (25&nbsp;mi) south-west of Antigua lies the small, rocky island of <a href="/wiki/Redonda" title="Redonda">Redonda</a>, which is uninhabited.<sup id="cite_ref-Britannica_12-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Britannica-12">[12]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cities_and_villages">Cities and villages</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Antigua_and_Barbuda&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Cities and villages">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Further information: <a href="/wiki/List_of_cities_in_Antigua_and_Barbuda" title="List of cities in Antigua and Barbuda">List of cities in Antigua and Barbuda</a>
      </div> 
      <p>The most populous cities in Antigua and Barbuda are mostly on Antigua, being <a href="/wiki/Saint_John%27s,_Antigua_and_Barbuda" class="mw-redirect" title="Saint John's, Antigua and Barbuda">Saint John's</a>, <a href="/wiki/All_Saints,_Antigua_and_Barbuda" title="All Saints, Antigua and Barbuda">All Saints</a>, <a href="/wiki/Piggotts" title="Piggotts">Piggotts</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Liberta,_Antigua_and_Barbuda" title="Liberta, Antigua and Barbuda">Liberta</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup> The most populous city on Barbuda is <a href="/wiki/Codrington,_Antigua_and_Barbuda" title="Codrington, Antigua and Barbuda">Codrington</a>. It is estimated that 25% of the population lives in an Urban area, which is much lower than the international average of 55%.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Islands">Islands</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Antigua_and_Barbuda&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Islands">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Further information: <a href="/wiki/Geography_of_Antigua_and_Barbuda#Islands" title="Geography of Antigua and Barbuda">Geography of Antigua and Barbuda §&nbsp;Islands</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Antigua and Barbuda is comprised mostly of its two namesake islands, <a href="/wiki/Antigua" title="Antigua">Antigua</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Barbuda" title="Barbuda">Barbuda</a>, other than that, Antigua and Barbuda's biggest islands are Guiana Island and Long Island off the coast of Antigua, and <a href="/wiki/Redonda" title="Redonda">Redonda</a> island, which is far from both of the main islands. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">Climate</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Antigua_and_Barbuda&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Climate">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>Rainfall averages 990&nbsp;mm (39&nbsp;in) per year, with the amount varying widely from season to season. In general the wettest period is between September and November. The islands generally experience low humidity and recurrent droughts. Temperatures average 27&nbsp;°C (80.6&nbsp;°F), with a range from 23&nbsp;°C (73.4&nbsp;°F) to 29&nbsp;°C (84.2&nbsp;°F) in the winter to from 25&nbsp;°C (77.0&nbsp;°F) to 30&nbsp;°C (86.0&nbsp;°F) in the summer and autumn. The coolest period is between December and February. </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Hurricane" class="mw-redirect" title="Hurricane">Hurricanes</a> strike on an average of once a year, including the powerful <a href="/wiki/Category_5_hurricane" class="mw-redirect" title="Category 5 hurricane">Category 5</a> <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Irma" title="Hurricane Irma">Hurricane Irma</a>, on 6 September 2017, which damaged 95% of the structures on Barbuda.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup> Some 1,800 people were evacuated to Antigua.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>An estimate published by <i><a href="/wiki/Time_(magazine)" title="Time (magazine)">Time</a></i> indicated that over $100&nbsp;million would be required to rebuild homes and infrastructure. Philmore Mullin, Director of Barbuda's National Office of Disaster Services, said that "all critical infrastructure and utilities are non-existent – food supply, medicine, shelter, electricity, water, communications, waste management". He summarised the situation as follows: "Public utilities need to be rebuilt in their entirety... It is optimistic to think anything can be rebuilt in six months ... In my 25 years in disaster management, I have never seen something like this."<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Environmental_issues">Environmental issues</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Antigua_and_Barbuda&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Environmental issues">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="excerpt-block">
       <style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r952607947">.mw-parser-output .excerpt .selflink{font-weight:normal}.mw-parser-output .excerpt-indicator{border-left:3px solid #c8ccd1;margin:1em 0;padding-left:1em}</style>
       <div class="dablink excerpt-hat">
        <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable dablink selfref">
         This section is an excerpt from <a href="/wiki/Environmental_issues_in_Antigua_and_Barbuda" title="Environmental issues in Antigua and Barbuda">Environmental issues in Antigua and Barbuda</a><i><span class="mw-editsection-like plainlinks"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Environmental_issues_in_Antigua_and_Barbuda&amp;action=edit">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></i>
        </div>
       </div>
       <div class="excerpt"> 
        <p>Like other <a href="/wiki/Island_country" title="Island country">island nations</a>, Antigua and Barbuda faces unique environmental issues created by its proximity to the ocean, and small size. These include pressures on water resources, natural ecosystems, and deforestation more generally. </p>
        <p>Existing issues on the island are further made worse by climate change, where, unlike other <a href="/wiki/Effects_of_climate_change_on_island_nations" title="Effects of climate change on island nations">island nations affected by climate change</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sea_level_rise" title="Sea level rise">sea level rise</a>, increased weather variability, create increased pressures on the communities on the islands and the land, through processes like <a href="/wiki/Coastal_erosion" title="Coastal erosion">coastal erosion</a> and <a href="/wiki/Saltwater_intrusion" title="Saltwater intrusion">saltwater intrusion</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup> </p> Not only do these issues threaten the residents of the island, but also interfere with the economy&nbsp;– where tourism is 80% of the GDP.<sup id="cite_ref-Environmental_issues_in_Antigua_and_Barbuda_:1_34-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Environmental_issues_in_Antigua_and_Barbuda_:1-34">[34]</a></sup> The 2017 hurricane season was particularly destructive, with <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Maria" title="Hurricane Maria">Hurricane Maria</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Irma" title="Hurricane Irma">Hurricane Irma</a>, repeatedly damaging vulnerable infrastructure on the islands of Antigua and Barbuda.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Antigua_and_Barbuda&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Demographics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Demographics_of_Antigua_and_Barbuda" title="Demographics of Antigua and Barbuda">Demographics of Antigua and Barbuda</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:452px;">

      </div> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ethnic_groups">Ethnic groups</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Antigua_and_Barbuda&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Ethnic groups">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>Antigua has a population of 96,286,<sup id="cite_ref-UN_WPP_2-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UN_WPP-2">[2]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-UN_WPP_2019_3-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UN_WPP_2019-3">[3]</a></sup> mostly made up of people of <a href="/wiki/West_African" class="mw-redirect" title="West African">West African</a>, British, and <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_people" title="Portuguese people">Madeiran</a> descent. The ethnic distribution consists of 91% Black &amp; Mulatto, 4.4% mixed race, 1.7% White, and 2.9% other (primarily <a href="/wiki/South_Asians" class="mw-redirect" title="South Asians">East Indian</a> and other Asian). Most Whites are of British descent. Christian Levantine Arabs, and a small number of <a href="/wiki/Asians" class="mw-redirect" title="Asians">Asians</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sephardic_Jews" class="mw-redirect" title="Sephardic Jews">Sephardic Jews</a> make up the remainder of the population. </p>
      <p>An increasingly large percentage of the population lives abroad, most notably in the United Kingdom (<a href="/wiki/Antiguan_British" class="mw-redirect" title="Antiguan British">Antiguan Britons</a>), United States and Canada. A minority of Antiguan residents are immigrants from other countries, particularly from Dominica, Guyana and <a href="/wiki/Jamaica" title="Jamaica">Jamaica</a>, and, increasingly, from the Dominican Republic, <a href="/wiki/St._Vincent_and_the_Grenadines" class="mw-redirect" title="St. Vincent and the Grenadines">St. Vincent and the Grenadines</a> and <a href="/wiki/Nigeria" title="Nigeria">Nigeria</a>. An estimated 4,500 American citizens also make their home in Antigua and Barbuda, making their numbers one of the largest American populations in the English-speaking Eastern Caribbean.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Languages">Languages</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Antigua_and_Barbuda&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Languages">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>English is the official language. The <a href="/wiki/Barbuda" title="Barbuda">Barbudan</a> accent is slightly different from the <a href="/wiki/Antigua" title="Antigua">Antiguan</a>. </p>
      <p>In the years before Antigua and Barbuda's independence, Standard English was widely spoken in preference to Antiguan Creole. Generally, the upper and middle classes shun Antiguan Creole. The educational system dissuades the use of Antiguan Creole and instruction is done in Standard (British) English. </p>
      <p>Many of the words used in the Antiguan dialect are derived from <a href="/wiki/British_English" title="British English">British</a> as well as African languages. This can be easily seen in phrases such as: "Ent it?" meaning "Ain't it?" which is itself dialectal and means "Isn't it?". Common island <a href="/wiki/Proverb" title="Proverb">proverbs</a> can often be traced to Africa. </p>
      <p>Spanish is spoken by around 10,000 inhabitants.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">Religion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Antigua_and_Barbuda&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Religion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Stjohnscathedralantigua.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/Stjohnscathedralantigua.jpg/220px-Stjohnscathedralantigua.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/Stjohnscathedralantigua.jpg/330px-Stjohnscathedralantigua.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/Stjohnscathedralantigua.jpg/440px-Stjohnscathedralantigua.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2304" data-file-height="1728"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Stjohnscathedralantigua.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/St._John%27s_Cathedral,_St._John%27s" class="mw-redirect" title="St. John's Cathedral, St. John's">St. John's Cathedral, St. John's</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>A majority (77%)<sup id="cite_ref-Factbook_1-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Factbook-1">[1]</a></sup> of Antiguans are Christians, with the <a href="/wiki/Anglicans" class="mw-redirect" title="Anglicans">Anglicans</a> (17.6%) being the largest single denomination. Other Christian denominations present are <a href="/wiki/Seventh-day_Adventist_Church" title="Seventh-day Adventist Church">Seventh-day Adventist Church</a> (12.4%), <a href="/wiki/Pentecostalism" title="Pentecostalism">Pentecostalism</a> (12.2%), <a href="/wiki/Moravian_Church" title="Moravian Church">Moravian Church</a> (8.3%), <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholics" class="mw-redirect" title="Roman Catholics">Roman Catholics</a> (8.2%), <a href="/wiki/Methodist_Church" class="mw-redirect" title="Methodist Church">Methodist Church</a> (5.6%), <a href="/wiki/Wesleyan_Holiness_Church" title="Wesleyan Holiness Church">Wesleyan Holiness Church</a> (4.5%), <a href="/wiki/Church_of_God_(Cleveland,_Tennessee)" title="Church of God (Cleveland, Tennessee)">Church of God</a> (4.1%), <a href="/wiki/Baptists" title="Baptists">Baptists</a> (3.6%),<sup id="cite_ref-FactbookAttribution_38-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FactbookAttribution-38">[38]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Mormonism" title="Mormonism">Mormonism</a> (&lt;1.0%), as well as <a href="/wiki/Jehovah%27s_Witnesses" title="Jehovah's Witnesses">Jehovah's Witnesses</a>. </p>
      <p>Non-Christian religions practiced in the islands include the <a href="/wiki/Rastafari" title="Rastafari">Rastafari</a>, <a href="/wiki/Islam" title="Islam">Islam</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Bah%C3%A1%CA%BC%C3%AD_Faith" title="Baháʼí Faith">Baháʼí Faith</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2019)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Governance">Governance</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Antigua_and_Barbuda&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Governance">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Political_system">Political system</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Antigua_and_Barbuda&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Political system">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Politics_of_Antigua_and_Barbuda" title="Politics of Antigua and Barbuda">Politics of Antigua and Barbuda</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:St_Johns_Antigua_2012.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/71/St_Johns_Antigua_2012.jpg/220px-St_Johns_Antigua_2012.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="133" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/71/St_Johns_Antigua_2012.jpg/330px-St_Johns_Antigua_2012.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/71/St_Johns_Antigua_2012.jpg/440px-St_Johns_Antigua_2012.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5421" data-file-height="3278"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:St_Johns_Antigua_2012.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>St. John's on Antigua.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The politics of Antigua and Barbuda take place within a framework of a <a href="/wiki/Unitary_state" title="Unitary state">unitary</a>, <a href="/wiki/Parliamentary_system" title="Parliamentary system">parliamentary</a>, <a href="/wiki/Representative_democracy" title="Representative democracy">representative democratic</a> monarchy, in which the <a href="/wiki/Head_of_State" class="mw-redirect" title="Head of State">head of State</a> is the monarch who appoints the <a href="/wiki/List_of_Governors-General_of_Antigua_and_Barbuda" class="mw-redirect" title="List of Governors-General of Antigua and Barbuda">Governor-General</a> as vice-regal representative.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Elizabeth_II" title="Elizabeth II">Elizabeth II</a> is the present <a href="/wiki/Queen_of_Antigua_and_Barbuda" class="mw-redirect" title="Queen of Antigua and Barbuda">Queen of Antigua and Barbuda</a>, having served in that position since the islands' independence from the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">United Kingdom</a> in 1981. The Queen is currently represented by Governor-General <a href="/wiki/Rodney_Williams_(politician)" class="mw-redirect" title="Rodney Williams (politician)">Sir Rodney Williams</a>. A council of ministers is appointed by the governor general on the advice of the <a href="/wiki/List_of_Prime_Ministers_of_Antigua_and_Barbuda" class="mw-redirect" title="List of Prime Ministers of Antigua and Barbuda">prime minister</a>, currently <a href="/wiki/Gaston_Browne" title="Gaston Browne">Gaston Browne</a> (2014–).<sup id="cite_ref-FactbookAttribution_38-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FactbookAttribution-38">[38]</a></sup> The prime minister is the <a href="/wiki/Head_of_government" title="Head of government">head of government</a>. </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Executive_power" class="mw-redirect" title="Executive power">Executive power</a> is exercised by the government while <a href="/wiki/Legislative_power" class="mw-redirect" title="Legislative power">legislative power</a> is vested in both the <a href="/wiki/Forms_of_government" class="mw-redirect" title="Forms of government">government</a> and the two Chambers of <a href="/wiki/Parliament_of_Antigua_and_Barbuda" title="Parliament of Antigua and Barbuda">Parliament</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Bicameral" class="mw-redirect" title="Bicameral">bicameral</a> Parliament consists of the Senate (17 members appointed by members of the government and the <a href="/wiki/Official_Opposition" class="mw-redirect" title="Official Opposition">opposition</a> party, and approved by the Governor-General), and the House of Representatives (17 members elected by <a href="/wiki/First_past_the_post" class="mw-redirect" title="First past the post">first past the post</a>) to serve five-year terms. </p>
      <p>The current Leader of Her Majesty's Loyal Opposition is the United Progressive Party Member of Parliament (MP), the Honourable <a href="/wiki/Baldwin_Spencer" title="Baldwin Spencer">Baldwin Spencer</a>. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Elections">Elections</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Antigua_and_Barbuda&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Elections">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Antigua.St.John.from_west.wmt.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/66/Antigua.St.John.from_west.wmt.jpg/220px-Antigua.St.John.from_west.wmt.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/66/Antigua.St.John.from_west.wmt.jpg/330px-Antigua.St.John.from_west.wmt.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/66/Antigua.St.John.from_west.wmt.jpg/440px-Antigua.St.John.from_west.wmt.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2000" data-file-height="1501"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Antigua.St.John.from_west.wmt.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>St. John's parish on Antigua.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The last elections held were on 12 June 2014, during which the <a href="/wiki/Antigua_Labour_Party" class="mw-redirect" title="Antigua Labour Party">Antigua Labour Party</a> won 14 seats, and the <a href="/wiki/United_Progressive_Party_(Antigua_and_Barbuda)" title="United Progressive Party (Antigua and Barbuda)">United Progressive Party</a> 3 seats. </p>
      <p>Since 1951, elections have been won by the <a href="/wiki/Populism" title="Populism">populist</a> Antigua Labour Party. However, in the <a href="/wiki/Antigua_and_Barbuda_general_election,_2004" class="mw-redirect" title="Antigua and Barbuda general election, 2004">Antigua and Barbuda legislative election of 2004</a> saw the defeat of the longest-serving elected government in the Caribbean. </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Vere_Bird" title="Vere Bird">Vere Bird</a> was Prime Minister from 1981 to 1994 and Chief Minister of Antigua from 1960 to 1981, except for the 1971–1976 period when the Progressive Labour Movement (PLM) defeated his party. Bird, the nation's first Prime Minister, is credited with having brought Antigua and Barbuda and the Caribbean into a new era of independence. Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Lester_Bird" title="Lester Bird">Lester Bryant Bird</a> succeeded the elder Bird in 1994. </p>
      <p><br> </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Party_elections">Party elections</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Antigua_and_Barbuda&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Party elections">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <p><a href="/wiki/Gaston_Browne" title="Gaston Browne">Gaston Browne</a> defeated his predecessor <a href="/wiki/Lester_Bryant_Bird" class="mw-redirect" title="Lester Bryant Bird">Lester Bryant Bird</a> at the Antigua Labour Party's biennial convention in November 2012 held to elect a political leader and other officers. The party then altered its name from the <a href="/wiki/Antigua_Labour_Party" class="mw-redirect" title="Antigua Labour Party">Antigua Labour Party</a> (ALP) to the Antigua and Barbuda Labour Party (ABLP). This was done to officially include the party's presence on the sister island of Barbuda in its organisation, the only political party on the mainland to have a physical branch in Barbuda. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Judiciary">Judiciary</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Antigua_and_Barbuda&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Judiciary">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>The Judicial branch is the <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Caribbean_Supreme_Court" title="Eastern Caribbean Supreme Court">Eastern Caribbean Supreme Court</a> (based in Saint Lucia; one judge of the Supreme Court is a resident of the islands and presides over the High Court of Justice). Antigua is also a member of the <a href="/wiki/Caribbean_Court_of_Justice" title="Caribbean Court of Justice">Caribbean Court of Justice</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Judicial_Committee_of_the_Privy_Council" title="Judicial Committee of the Privy Council">Judicial Committee of the Privy Council</a> serves as its Supreme Court of Appeal.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Foreign_relations">Foreign relations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Antigua_and_Barbuda&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Foreign relations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Foreign_relations_of_Antigua_and_Barbuda" title="Foreign relations of Antigua and Barbuda">Foreign relations of Antigua and Barbuda</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Antigua and Barbuda is a member of the United Nations, the <a href="/wiki/Bolivarian_Alliance_for_the_Americas" class="mw-redirect" title="Bolivarian Alliance for the Americas">Bolivarian Alliance for the Americas</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_of_Nations" title="Commonwealth of Nations">Commonwealth of Nations</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Caribbean_Community" title="Caribbean Community">Caribbean Community</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Organization_of_Eastern_Caribbean_States" class="mw-redirect" title="Organization of Eastern Caribbean States">Organization of Eastern Caribbean States</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Organization_of_American_States" title="Organization of American States">Organization of American States</a>, the <a href="/wiki/World_Trade_Organization" title="World Trade Organization">World Trade Organization</a> and the Eastern Caribbean's Regional Security System. </p>
      <p>Antigua and Barbuda is also a member of the <a href="/wiki/International_Criminal_Court" title="International Criminal Court">International Criminal Court</a> (with a <a href="/wiki/Bilateral_Immunity_Agreement" class="mw-redirect" title="Bilateral Immunity Agreement">Bilateral Immunity Agreement</a> of Protection for the US military as covered under Article 98 of the <a href="/wiki/Rome_Statute_of_the_International_Criminal_Court" title="Rome Statute of the International Criminal Court">Rome Statute</a>). </p>
      <p>In 2013, Antigua and Barbuda called for <a href="/wiki/Reparations_for_slavery" title="Reparations for slavery">reparations for slavery</a> at the United Nations. Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Baldwin_Spencer" title="Baldwin Spencer">Baldwin Spencer</a> said "We have recently seen a number of leaders apologising", and that they should now "match their words with concrete and material benefits."<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Military">Military</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Antigua_and_Barbuda&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Military">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Further information: <a href="/wiki/Royal_Antigua_and_Barbuda_Defence_Force" title="Royal Antigua and Barbuda Defence Force">Royal Antigua and Barbuda Defence Force</a>
      </div> 
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Royal_Antigua_and_Barbuda_Defence_Force" title="Royal Antigua and Barbuda Defence Force">Royal Antigua and Barbuda Defence Force</a> has around 260 members dispersed between the line infantry regiment, service and support unit and coast guard. There is also the Antigua and Barbuda Cadet Corps made up of 200 teenagers between the ages of 12 to 18. </p>
      <p>In 2018, Antigua and Barbuda signed the UN <a href="/wiki/Treaty_on_the_Prohibition_of_Nuclear_Weapons" title="Treaty on the Prohibition of Nuclear Weapons">treaty on the Prohibition of Nuclear Weapons</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Administrative_divisions">Administrative divisions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Antigua_and_Barbuda&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Administrative divisions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Parishes_and_dependencies_of_Antigua_and_Barbuda" title="Parishes and dependencies of Antigua and Barbuda">Parishes and dependencies of Antigua and Barbuda</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Antigua and Barbuda is divided into six parishes and two dependencies:<sup id="cite_ref-FactbookAttribution_38-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FactbookAttribution-38">[38]</a></sup> </p>

               <div style="position: absolute;font-size:100%;left:260px;top:260px">
                <a href="/wiki/Saint_Peter_Parish,_Antigua_and_Barbuda" title="Saint Peter Parish, Antigua and Barbuda">St. Peter</a>
               </div> 
               <div style="position: absolute;font-size:100%;left:260px;top:283px">
                <a href="/wiki/Saint_Philip_Parish,_Antigua_and_Barbuda" title="Saint Philip Parish, Antigua and Barbuda">St. Philip</a>
               </div>

               <div style="position: absolute;font-size:100%;left:90px;top:160px">
