           </tbody>
          </table> </td>
        </tr>
       </tbody>
      </table> 
      <p>Note: Though Barbuda and Redonda are called dependencies they are integral parts of the state, making them essentially administrative divisions. Dependency is simply a title. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Human_rights">Human rights</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Antigua_and_Barbuda&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Human rights">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>Antigua and Barbuda does not allow discrimination in employment, child labor, <a href="/wiki/Human_trafficking" title="Human trafficking">human trafficking</a>, and there are laws against <a href="/wiki/Domestic_abuse" class="mw-redirect" title="Domestic abuse">domestic abuse</a> and <a href="/wiki/Child_abuse" title="Child abuse">child abuse</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup> Although it has not been enforced or a case brought to trial in many years, like other Caribbean islands, <a href="/wiki/LGBT_rights_in_Antigua_and_Barbuda" title="LGBT rights in Antigua and Barbuda">same-sex sexual activity</a> is illegal in Antigua and Barbuda and punishable by prison time. There are several current movements under way to repeal the buggery laws.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Antigua_and_Barbuda&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Economy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Antigua_and_Barbuda" title="Economy of Antigua and Barbuda">Economy of Antigua and Barbuda</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Tourism dominates the economy, accounting for more than half of the gross domestic product (GDP).<sup id="cite_ref-Factbook_1-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Factbook-1">[1]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Britannica_12-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Britannica-12">[12]</a></sup> Antigua is famous for its many luxury resorts as an ultra-high end travel destination. Weakened tourist activity in the lower and middle market segments since early 2000 has slowed the economy, however, and squeezed the government into a tight fiscal corner.<sup id="cite_ref-Factbook_1-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Factbook-1">[1]</a></sup> Antigua and Barbuda has enacted policies to attract high-net worth citizens and resident, such as enacting a 0% personal income tax rate in 2019.<sup id="cite_ref-auto1_11-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto1-11">[11]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Investment banking and financial services also make up an important part of the economy. Major world banks with offices in Antigua include the Royal Bank of Canada (RBC) and Scotiabank. Financial-services corporations with offices in Antigua include PriceWaterhouseCoopers. The <a href="/wiki/US_Securities_and_Exchange_Commission" class="mw-redirect" title="US Securities and Exchange Commission">US Securities and Exchange Commission</a> has accused the Antigua-based <a href="/wiki/Stanford_International_Bank" title="Stanford International Bank">Stanford International Bank</a>, owned by Texas billionaire <a href="/wiki/Allen_Stanford" title="Allen Stanford">Allen Stanford</a>, of orchestrating a huge fraud which may have bilked investors of some $8&nbsp;billion.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The twin-island nation's agricultural production is focused on its domestic market and constrained by a limited <a href="/wiki/Water_supply" title="Water supply">water supply</a> and a <a href="/wiki/Labor_(economics)" class="mw-redirect" title="Labor (economics)">labour</a> shortage stemming from the lure of higher wages in tourism and construction work.<sup id="cite_ref-FactbookAttribution_38-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FactbookAttribution-38">[38]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Manufacturing is made up of enclave-type assembly for export, the major products being bedding, handicrafts and electronic components. Prospects for economic growth in the medium term will continue to depend on income growth in the industrialised world, especially in the United States,<sup id="cite_ref-FactbookAttribution_38-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FactbookAttribution-38">[38]</a></sup> from which about one-third of all tourists come.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2019)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p>
      <p>Access to <a href="/wiki/Biocapacity" title="Biocapacity">biocapacity</a> is lower than world average. In 2016, Antigua and Barbuda had 0.8 global hectares<sup id="cite_ref-footprintdata_47-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-footprintdata-47">[47]</a></sup> of biocapacity per person within its territory, much less than the world average of 1.6 global hectares per person.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup> In 2016 Antigua and Barbuda used 4.3 global hectares of biocapacity per person - their <a href="/wiki/Ecological_footprint" title="Ecological footprint">ecological footprint</a> of consumption. This means they use more biocapacity than Antigua and Barbuda contains. As a result, Antigua and Barbuda are running a biocapacity deficit.<sup id="cite_ref-footprintdata_47-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-footprintdata-47">[47]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Following the opening of the American University of Antigua College of Medicine by investor and attorney Neil Simon in 2003, a new source of revenue was established. The university employs many local Antiguans and the approximate 1000 students consume a large amount of the goods and services.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2019)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p>
      <p>Antigua and Barbuda also uses an <a href="/wiki/Economic_citizenship" title="Economic citizenship">economic citizenship</a> program to spur investment into the country.<sup id="cite_ref-CIU_49-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIU-49">[49]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Transport">Transport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Antigua_and_Barbuda&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Transport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="excerpt-block">
       <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r952607947">
       <div class="dablink excerpt-hat">
        <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable dablink selfref">
         This section is an excerpt from <a href="/wiki/Transport_in_Antigua_and_Barbuda" title="Transport in Antigua and Barbuda">Transport in Antigua and Barbuda</a><i><span class="mw-editsection-like plainlinks"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Transport_in_Antigua_and_Barbuda&amp;action=edit">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></i>
        </div>
       </div>
       <div class="excerpt"> 
        <table class="box-CIA plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-style" role="presentation">
         <tbody>
          <tr>
           <td class="mbox-image">
            <div style="width:52px">
             <img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/f2/Edit-clear.svg/40px-Edit-clear.svg.png" decoding="async" width="40" height="40" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/f2/Edit-clear.svg/60px-Edit-clear.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/f2/Edit-clear.svg/80px-Edit-clear.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="48" data-file-height="48">
            </div></td>
           <td class="mbox-text">
            <div class="mbox-text-span">
             This article was <b><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Status_of_the_porting_of_the_CIA_World_Factbook" title="Wikipedia:Status of the porting of the CIA World Factbook">imported from the CIA World Factbook</a></b> and may require rewriting and/or reformatting to meet Wikipedia's <a href="/wiki/Category:Wikipedia_style_guidelines" title="Category:Wikipedia style guidelines">quality standards</a>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please discuss this issue on the <a href="/wiki/Talk:Antigua_and_Barbuda" title="Talk:Antigua and Barbuda">talk page</a>. <a href="/wiki/Help:Editing" title="Help:Editing">Editing help</a> is available.</span><small class="hide-when-compact"><i> (<a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a>)</i></small>
            </div></td>
          </tr>
         </tbody>
        </table> 
        <p><a href="/wiki/Transport_in_Antigua_and_Barbuda" title="Transport in Antigua and Barbuda">Antigua and Barbuda's transport</a> systems include both public and privately run services. <a href="/wiki/Road" title="Road">Roads</a> in the country are paved and follow a winding and gently sloping course connecting parishes to villages and communities. Driving is on the left-hand side. The speed limit is set at 40&nbsp;mph, Traffic signs posted throughout main roads in Antigua and Barbuda allow for ease of commute, and with GPS coordinates posted throughout the country, the process of navigation has become even easier. </p>
        <p><a href="/wiki/Public_transportation" class="mw-redirect" title="Public transportation">Public transportation</a> vehicles contain the letters "BUS" for buses or "TX" for taxis on their yellow <a href="/wiki/Licence_plate" class="mw-redirect" title="Licence plate">licence plates</a>. The government regulates <a href="/wiki/Taxi_cab" class="mw-redirect" title="Taxi cab">taxi</a> service, setting fixed fares rather than using a metered system. Taxi cabs are supposed to keep a copy of the rates inside the vehicle. On Antigua, taxis are easily found, particularly at the airport and at major hotels. Many taxi drivers also will act as tour guides. </p> <a href="/wiki/Bus" title="Bus">Buses</a> operate from 5:30&nbsp;a.m. to 6:00&nbsp;p.m. daily on Antigua, running between the capital city, <a href="/wiki/St._John%27s,_Antigua_and_Barbuda" title="St. John's, Antigua and Barbuda">St. John's</a>, and various villages. However, buses do not stop at the <a href="/wiki/Airport" title="Airport">airport</a> or the northern tourist area. Although departure times are often left up to the driver, buses generally follow a set schedule. Most buses have their routes posted in the front windows, and they're usually privately owned mini-vans seating about 15 people. St. John's has two bus stations, the East Bus Station near the Botanical Gardens on Independence Ave and another one on Market St. near the Central Market. Several buses are also available on Barbuda.
       </div>
      </div> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Antigua_and_Barbuda&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div class="excerpt-block">
       <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r952607947">
       <div class="dablink excerpt-hat">
        <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable dablink selfref">
         This section is an excerpt from <a href="/wiki/Education_in_Antigua_and_Barbuda" title="Education in Antigua and Barbuda">Education in Antigua and Barbuda</a><i><span class="mw-editsection-like plainlinks"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Education_in_Antigua_and_Barbuda&amp;action=edit">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></i>
        </div>
       </div>
       <div class="excerpt"> 
        <p><a href="/wiki/Education_in_Antigua_and_Barbuda" title="Education in Antigua and Barbuda">Education in Antigua and Barbuda</a> is compulsory and free for children between the ages of 5 and 16 years.<sup id="cite_ref-Education_in_Antigua_and_Barbuda_ilab_50-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Education_in_Antigua_and_Barbuda_ilab-50">[50]</a></sup> The system of education in Antigua and Barbuda is based on the British educational system. The school year begins in September and ends in June of the following year. In order to ensure that all costs related to schooling are covered by the government, there is an education levy on all basic wages in Antigua and Barbuda, with the funds used toward such costs as supplies, transportation, and school infrastructure maintenance.<sup id="cite_ref-Education_in_Antigua_and_Barbuda_ilab_50-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Education_in_Antigua_and_Barbuda_ilab-50">[50]</a></sup> Primary education begins at the age of five years and normally lasts for seven years. Secondary education lasts for five years, with three years of lower secondary, followed by two years of upper secondary. In 2001, there were about 13,000 students enrolled at the primary schools and 5,000 students at the secondary schools. About 1,000 secondary school age students were enrolled in vocational programs. As of 2000, the primary pupil-teacher ratio was an estimated 19 to 1; the ratio for secondary school was about 13:1. The <a href="/wiki/Government_of_Antigua_and_Barbuda" class="mw-redirect" title="Government of Antigua and Barbuda">government</a> administers the majority of the schools, including 42 public schools and 45 private schools.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">[51]</a></sup> In 2003, estimated spending on education was about 3.8% of the <a href="/wiki/GDP" class="mw-redirect" title="GDP">GDP</a>. In 2000, about 38% of primary school students were enrolled in private schools. </p> 
        <div class="thumb tright">
         <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Aid_to_Basic_Education,_the_amount_of_bilateral_and_multilateral_aid_contributed_or_received_by_Antigua_and_Barbuda.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/Aid_to_Basic_Education%2C_the_amount_of_bilateral_and_multilateral_aid_contributed_or_received_by_Antigua_and_Barbuda.png/220px-Aid_to_Basic_Education%2C_the_amount_of_bilateral_and_multilateral_aid_contributed_or_received_by_Antigua_and_Barbuda.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="120" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/Aid_to_Basic_Education%2C_the_amount_of_bilateral_and_multilateral_aid_contributed_or_received_by_Antigua_and_Barbuda.png/330px-Aid_to_Basic_Education%2C_the_amount_of_bilateral_and_multilateral_aid_contributed_or_received_by_Antigua_and_Barbuda.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/Aid_to_Basic_Education%2C_the_amount_of_bilateral_and_multilateral_aid_contributed_or_received_by_Antigua_and_Barbuda.png/440px-Aid_to_Basic_Education%2C_the_amount_of_bilateral_and_multilateral_aid_contributed_or_received_by_Antigua_and_Barbuda.png 2x" data-file-width="1135" data-file-height="621"></a> 
          <div class="thumbcaption">
           <div class="magnify">
            <a href="/wiki/File:Aid_to_Basic_Education,_the_amount_of_bilateral_and_multilateral_aid_contributed_or_received_by_Antigua_and_Barbuda.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
           </div>Aid to Basic Education, the amount of bilateral and multilateral aid contributed or received by Antigua and Barbuda (source:UNESCO)
          </div>
         </div>
        </div> 
        <p>In 1972, the technical and teacher’s training colleges merged and formed the <a href="/wiki/Antigua_State_College" title="Antigua State College">Antigua State College</a>. Additional training options outside of university are offered at the Antigua and Barbuda Institute of Information Technology (ABIIT) and the Antigua and Barbuda Hospitality Training Institute (ABHTI). </p>
        <p>In 2019, the <a href="/wiki/University_of_the_West_Indies" title="University of the West Indies">University of the West Indies</a> opened its fifth campus overall (and fourth physical campus) in <a href="/wiki/University_of_the_West_Indies_at_Five_Islands" title="University of the West Indies at Five Islands">Five Islands</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup> The country was previously served solely by the <a href="/wiki/University_of_the_West_Indies" title="University of the West Indies">University of the West Indies</a> Open Campus.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">[53]</a></sup> The government of Antigua and Barbuda contributes financially to the UWI. </p>
        <p>The island of Antigua currently has three foreign-owned <a href="/wiki/For-profit_education" title="For-profit education">for-profit</a> <a href="/wiki/Offshore_medical_school" title="Offshore medical school">offshore medical schools</a>. The island's medical schools cater mostly to foreign students but contribute to the local economy and health care. The three schools are: </p> 
        <ul>
         <li>The <a href="/wiki/American_University_of_Antigua,_College_of_Medicine" class="mw-redirect" title="American University of Antigua, College of Medicine">American University of Antigua</a> (AUA),<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup> founded in 2004</li> 
         <li>The <a href="/wiki/University_of_Health_Sciences_Antigua" class="mw-redirect" title="University of Health Sciences Antigua">University of Health Sciences Antigua</a> (UHSA),<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">[55]</a></sup> founded in 1982</li> 
         <li>The <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.metropolitanmedschool.net/">Metropolitan University College of Medicine</a>.</li>
        </ul> Those interested in higher education also enroll at schools in the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">United Kingdom</a>, the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a>, <a href="/wiki/Europe" title="Europe">Europe</a> and <a href="/wiki/Canada" title="Canada">Canada</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Adult_literacy_rate" class="mw-redirect" title="Adult literacy rate">adult literacy rate</a> is approximately 89%.
       </div>
      </div> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Antigua_and_Barbuda&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <p>The culture is predominantly a mixture of West African and British cultural influences. </p>
      <p>Cricket is the national sport. Other popular sports include football, boat racing and surfing. (<a href="/wiki/Antigua_Sailing_Week" title="Antigua Sailing Week">Antigua Sailing Week</a> attracts locals and visitors from all over the world). </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Music">Music</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Antigua_and_Barbuda&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Music">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="excerpt-block">
       <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r952607947">
       <div class="dablink excerpt-hat">
        <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable dablink selfref">
         This section is an excerpt from <a href="/wiki/Music_of_Antigua_and_Barbuda" title="Music of Antigua and Barbuda">Music of Antigua and Barbuda</a><i><span class="mw-editsection-like plainlinks"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Music_of_Antigua_and_Barbuda&amp;action=edit">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></i>
        </div>
       </div>
       <div class="excerpt"> 
        <table class="box-More_citations_needed plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Refimprove" role="presentation">
         <tbody>
          <tr>
           <td class="mbox-image">
            <div style="width:52px">
             <a href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" decoding="async" width="50" height="39" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="512" data-file-height="399"></a>
            </div></td>
           <td class="mbox-text">
            <div class="mbox-text-span">
             This article <b>needs additional citations for <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">verification</a></b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please help <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Antigua_and_Barbuda&amp;action=edit">improve this article</a> by <a href="/wiki/Help:Referencing_for_beginners" title="Help:Referencing for beginners">adding citations to reliable sources</a>.             </div></td>
          </tr>
         </tbody>
        </table> 
        <p>The <a href="/wiki/Music_of_Antigua_and_Barbuda" title="Music of Antigua and Barbuda">music of Antigua and Barbuda</a> is largely African in character, and has only felt a limited influence from European styles due to the <a href="/wiki/Demographics_of_Antigua_and_Barbuda" title="Demographics of Antigua and Barbuda">population of Antigua and Barbuda</a> descending mostly from West Africans who were made slaves by Europeans.<sup id="cite_ref-Music_of_Antigua_and_Barbuda_Garland_56-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Music_of_Antigua_and_Barbuda_Garland-56">[56]</a></sup> </p>
        <p>Antigua and Barbuda is a Caribbean nation in the <a href="/wiki/Lesser_Antilles" title="Lesser Antilles">Lesser Antilles</a> island chain. The country is a second home for many of the pan-Caribbean genres of <a href="/wiki/Popular_music" title="Popular music">popular music</a>, and has produced stars in <a href="/wiki/Calypso_music" title="Calypso music">calypso</a>, <a href="/wiki/Soca_music" title="Soca music">soca</a>, <a href="/wiki/Steeldrum" class="mw-redirect" title="Steeldrum">steeldrum</a>, <a href="/wiki/Zouk_(musical_movement)" class="mw-redirect" title="Zouk (musical movement)">zouk</a> and <a href="/wiki/Reggae" title="Reggae">reggae</a>. Of these, steeldrum and calypso are the most integral parts of modern Antiguan popular music; both styles are imported from the <a href="/wiki/Music_of_Trinidad_and_Tobago" title="Music of Trinidad and Tobago">music of Trinidad and Tobago</a>. </p> Little to no musical research has been undertaken on Antigua and Barbuda. As a result, much knowledge on the topic derives from novels, essays and other secondary sources.<sup id="cite_ref-Music_of_Antigua_and_Barbuda_Garland_56-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Music_of_Antigua_and_Barbuda_Garland-56">[56]</a></sup>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Festivals">Festivals</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Antigua_and_Barbuda&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Festivals">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>The national Carnival held each August commemorates the abolition of slavery in the <a href="/wiki/British_West_Indies" title="British West Indies">British West Indies</a>, although on some islands, Carnival may celebrate the coming of Lent. Its festive pageants, shows, contests and other activities are a major tourist attraction. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cuisine">Cuisine</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Antigua_and_Barbuda&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Cuisine">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="excerpt-block">
       <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r952607947">
       <div class="dablink excerpt-hat">
        <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable dablink selfref">
         This section is an excerpt from <a href="/wiki/Antigua_and_Barbuda_cuisine" title="Antigua and Barbuda cuisine">Antigua and Barbuda cuisine</a><i><span class="mw-editsection-like plainlinks"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Antigua_and_Barbuda_cuisine&amp;action=edit">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></i>
        </div>
       </div>
       <div class="excerpt"> 
        <table class="box-Tone plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-style ambox-Tone" role="presentation">
         <tbody>
          <tr>
           <td class="mbox-image">
            <div style="width:52px">
             <img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/f2/Edit-clear.svg/40px-Edit-clear.svg.png" decoding="async" width="40" height="40" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/f2/Edit-clear.svg/60px-Edit-clear.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/f2/Edit-clear.svg/80px-Edit-clear.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="48" data-file-height="48">
            </div></td>
           <td class="mbox-text">
            <div class="mbox-text-span">
             This article's <b>tone or style may not reflect the <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Writing_better_articles#Tone" title="Wikipedia:Writing better articles">encyclopedic tone</a> used on Wikipedia</b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> See Wikipedia's <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Writing_better_articles#Tone" title="Wikipedia:Writing better articles">guide to writing better articles</a> for suggestions.</span> <small class="date-container"><i>(<span class="date">January 2017</span>)</i></small><small class="hide-when-compact"><i> (<a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a>)</i></small>
            </div></td>
          </tr>
         </tbody>
        </table> 
        <p><a href="/wiki/Antigua_and_Barbuda_cuisine" title="Antigua and Barbuda cuisine">Antigua and Barbuda cuisine</a> refers to the cuisines of the <a href="/wiki/Caribbean" title="Caribbean">Caribbean</a> <a href="/wiki/Island" title="Island">islands</a> <a href="/wiki/Antigua" title="Antigua">Antigua</a> and <a href="/wiki/Barbuda" title="Barbuda">Barbuda</a>. The national dish is <a href="/wiki/Cou-cou" title="Cou-cou">fungie</a> (pronounced "foon-jee") and pepperpot.<sup id="cite_ref-Antigua_and_Barbuda_cuisine_recipeisland_57-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Antigua_and_Barbuda_cuisine_recipeisland-57">[57]</a></sup> Fungie is a dish similar to Italian <a href="/wiki/Polenta" title="Polenta">Polenta</a>, made mostly with cornmeal.<sup id="cite_ref-Antigua_and_Barbuda_cuisine_recipeisland_57-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Antigua_and_Barbuda_cuisine_recipeisland-57">[57]</a></sup> Other local dishes include <a href="/wiki/Ducana" title="Ducana">ducana</a>, seasoned rice, <a href="/wiki/Saltfish" class="mw-redirect" title="Saltfish">saltfish</a> and <a href="/wiki/Lobster" title="Lobster">lobster</a> (from Barbuda). There are also local confectionaries which include: <a href="/wiki/Sugar_cake" title="Sugar cake">sugar cake</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fudge" title="Fudge">fudge</a>, raspberry and <a href="/wiki/Tamarind" title="Tamarind">tamarind</a> stew and <a href="/wiki/Peanut_brittle" class="mw-redirect" title="Peanut brittle">peanut brittle</a>. </p> 
        <div class="thumb tright">
         <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Jerk_chicken_july_05.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c2/Jerk_chicken_july_05.jpg/220px-Jerk_chicken_july_05.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c2/Jerk_chicken_july_05.jpg/330px-Jerk_chicken_july_05.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c2/Jerk_chicken_july_05.jpg/440px-Jerk_chicken_july_05.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2272" data-file-height="1704"></a> 
          <div class="thumbcaption">
           <div class="magnify">
            <a href="/wiki/File:Jerk_chicken_july_05.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
           </div><a href="/wiki/Jamaican_jerk_spice" class="mw-redirect" title="Jamaican jerk spice">Jerk chicken cooking</a>
          </div>
         </div>
        </div> Although these foods are indigenous to Antigua and Barbuda and to some other Caribbean countries, the local diet has diversified and now include local dishes of Jamaica, such as <a href="/wiki/Jamaican_jerk_spice" class="mw-redirect" title="Jamaican jerk spice">jerk meats</a>, or <a href="/wiki/Trinidad" title="Trinidad">Trinidad</a>, such as <a href="/wiki/Roti" title="Roti">Roti</a>, and other Caribbean countries.
       </div>
      </div> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Media">Media</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Antigua_and_Barbuda&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Media">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_newspapers_in_Antigua_and_Barbuda" title="List of newspapers in Antigua and Barbuda">List of newspapers in Antigua and Barbuda</a>
      </div> 
      <p>There are three newspapers: the <i>Antigua Daily Observer, Antigua New Room and The Antiguan Times.</i> The Antigua Observer is the only daily printed newspaper.<sup id="cite_ref-Media_58-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Media-58">[58]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The local television channel ABS TV 10 is available (it is the only station that shows exclusively local programs). There are also several local and regional radio stations, such as V2C-AM 620, ZDK-AM 1100, VYBZ-FM 92.9, ZDK-FM 97.1, Observer Radio 91.1 FM, DNECA Radio 90.1 FM, Second Advent Radio 101.5 FM, Abundant Life Radio 103.9 FM, Crusader Radio 107.3 FM, Nice FM 104.3.<sup id="cite_ref-Media_58-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Media-58">[58]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Literature">Literature</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Antigua_and_Barbuda&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Literature">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>Antiguan author <a href="/wiki/Jamaica_Kincaid" title="Jamaica Kincaid">Jamaica Kincaid</a> has published over 20 works of literature.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Sports">Sports</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Antigua_and_Barbuda&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Sports">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/Cricket_in_the_West_Indies" title="Cricket in the West Indies">Cricket in the West Indies</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Cricket_ground.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/Cricket_ground.jpg/220px-Cricket_ground.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/Cricket_ground.jpg/330px-Cricket_ground.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/Cricket_ground.jpg/440px-Cricket_ground.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2100" data-file-height="1400"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Cricket_ground.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The <a href="/wiki/Antigua_Recreation_Ground" title="Antigua Recreation Ground">Antigua Recreation Ground</a>.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Antigua_and_Barbuda_national_cricket_team" title="Antigua and Barbuda national cricket team">Antigua and Barbuda national cricket team</a> represented the country at the <a href="/wiki/1998_Commonwealth_Games" title="1998 Commonwealth Games">1998 Commonwealth Games</a>, but Antiguan cricketers otherwise play for the <a href="/wiki/Leeward_Islands_cricket_team" title="Leeward Islands cricket team">Leeward Islands cricket team</a> in domestic matches and the <a href="/wiki/West_Indies_cricket_team" title="West Indies cricket team">West Indies cricket team</a> internationally. The <a href="/wiki/2007_Cricket_World_Cup" title="2007 Cricket World Cup">2007 Cricket World Cup</a> was hosted in the West Indies from 11 March to 28 April 2007. </p>
      <p>Antigua hosted eight matches at the <a href="/wiki/Sir_Vivian_Richards_Stadium" title="Sir Vivian Richards Stadium">Sir Vivian Richards Stadium</a>, which was completed on 11 February 2007 and can hold up to 20,000 people. Antigua is a Host of <a href="/wiki/Stanford_Twenty20" class="mw-redirect" title="Stanford Twenty20">Stanford Twenty20</a> – <a href="/wiki/Twenty20_Cricket" class="mw-redirect" title="Twenty20 Cricket">Twenty20 Cricket</a>, a version started by <a href="/wiki/Allen_Stanford" title="Allen Stanford">Allen Stanford</a> in 2006 as a regional cricket game with almost all Caribbean islands taking part. <a href="/wiki/Rugby_football" title="Rugby football">Rugby</a> and <a href="/wiki/Netball" title="Netball">netball</a> are popular as well. </p>
      <p>Association football, or soccer, is also a very popular sport. Antigua has a <a href="/wiki/Antigua_and_Barbuda_national_football_team" title="Antigua and Barbuda national football team">national football team</a> which entered <a href="/wiki/FIFA_World_Cup_qualification" title="FIFA World Cup qualification">World Cup qualification</a> for the 1974 tournament and for 1986 and onwards. A professional team was formed in 2011, <a href="/wiki/Antigua_Barracuda_FC" title="Antigua Barracuda FC">Antigua Barracuda FC</a>, which played in the <a href="/wiki/USL_Pro" class="mw-redirect" title="USL Pro">USL Pro</a>, a lower professional league in the USA. The nation's team had a major achievement in 2012, getting out of its preliminary group for the 2014 <a href="/wiki/FIFA_World_Cup" title="FIFA World Cup">World Cup</a>, notably due to a victory over powerful <a href="/wiki/Haiti" title="Haiti">Haiti</a>. In its first game in the next <a href="/wiki/CONCACAF" title="CONCACAF">CONCACAF</a> group play on 8 June 2012 in <a href="/wiki/Tampa" class="mw-redirect" title="Tampa">Tampa</a>, FL, Antigua and Barbuda, comprising 17 Barracuda players and 7 from the lower English professional leagues, scored a goal against the United States. However, the team lost 3:1 to the US. </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Symbols">Symbols</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Antigua_and_Barbuda&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Symbols">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <p>The national bird is the <a href="/wiki/Frigate_bird" class="mw-redirect" title="Frigate bird">frigate bird</a>, and the national tree is the <a href="/wiki/Bucida_buceras" class="mw-redirect" title="Bucida buceras">Bucida buceras</a> (Whitewood tree).<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">[59]</a></sup> </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Clare_Waight_Keller" title="Clare Waight Keller">Clare Waight Keller</a> included <a href="/wiki/Agave" title="Agave">agave</a> karatto to represent Antigua and Barbuda in <a href="/wiki/Meghan_Markle" class="mw-redirect" title="Meghan Markle">Meghan Markle</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Wedding_of_Prince_Harry_and_Meghan_Markle" title="Wedding of Prince Harry and Meghan Markle">wedding</a> veil, which included the distinctive flora of each <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_of_Nations" title="Commonwealth of Nations">Commonwealth</a> country.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">[60]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Antigua_and_Barbuda&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: See also">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Further_reading">Further reading</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Antigua_and_Barbuda&amp;action=edit&amp;section=39" title="Edit section: Further reading">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <ul>
       <li>Nicholson, Desmond V., <i>Antigua, Barbuda, and Redonda: A Historical Sketch,</i> St. Johns, Antigua: Antigua and Barbuda Museum, 1991.</li> 
       <li>Dyde, Brian, <i>A History of Antigua: The Unsuspected Isle,</i> London: Macmillan Caribbean, 2000.</li> 
       <li>Gaspar, David Barry - <i>Bondmen &amp; Rebels: A Study of Master-Slave Relations in Antigua, with Implications for Colonial America.</i></li> 
       <li>Harris, David R. - <i>Plants, Animals, and Man in the Outer Leeward Islands, West Indies. An Ecological Study of Antigua, Barbuda, and Anguilla.</i></li> 
       <li>Henry, Paget - <i>Peripheral Capitalism and Underdevelopment in Antigua.</i></li> 
       <li>Lazarus-Black, Mindie - <i>Legitimate Acts and Illegal Encounters: Law and Society in Antigua and Barbuda.</i></li> 
       <li>Riley, J. H. - <i>Catalogue of a Collection of Birds from Barbuda and Antigua, British West Indies.</i></li> 
       <li>Rouse, Irving and Birgit Faber Morse - <i>Excavations at the Indian Creek Site, Antigua, West Indies.</i></li> 
       <li>Thomas Hearne. <i>Southampton.</i></li>
      </ul>
